Exit Site
If you are in danger, call 911. If you need to exit this website quickly, click on the ESCAPE button. This button will immediately open a browser window for weather.com and replace your current window with google.com.

## The .gov means it's official. 
Local, state, and federal government websites often end in .gov. Commonwealth of Pennsylvania government websites and email systems use "pennsylvania.gov" or "pa.gov" at the end of the address. Before sharing sensitive or personal information, make sure you're on an official state website.

  4. [ Medical Marijuana ](https://www.pa.gov/agencies/health/programs/medical-marijuana)
  5. Act 63


# Act 63 of 2023
On December 14, 2023, Governor Shapiro signed Act 63 of 2023 into law and it became effective April 12, 2024. Act 63 of 2023 allows qualified independent MMOs to apply for either a grower/processor (G/P) permit or dispensary permit: an independent G/P may apply for one dispensary permit and an independent dispensary may apply for one G/P permit. 
Act 63 to requires the permit granted as part of this application to be issued to the business entity that holds the original permit (the permittee). Therefore, the permit will not be issued to a separate, distinct legal entity. 
Applications for the additional permits and supporting documentation are listed in the latest phase when available.
[BMM Act 63 Questions and Answers](https://www.pa.gov/content/dam/copapwp-pagov/en/health/documents/topics/documents/programs/medical-marijuana/phase-1/BMM%20Act%2063%20QA.pdf), 6/5/2024 Update (PDF)
###  Phase 3 – Fall of 2025 (closed)

IF A PRINCIPAL, FINANCIAL BACKER, OR OPERATOR IS A BUSINESS ENTITY, PLEASE LIST THE NATURAL PERSON WHO IS OR WILL BE AFFILIATED ON BEHALF OF THAT ENTITY AND PROVIDE THE NAME OF THE ENTITY IN COLUMN F FOR EACH NATURAL PERSON.

Daniel J. Asti, RPh Founder and CEO
* * *
After graduating from Duquesne University School of Pharmacy in 1995, Dan began his career working for Thrift Drug in the community pharmacy setting. During his tenure working in the corporate pharmacy world, he operated some of the Chain’s highest volume pharmacies and was awarded for his success in restoring proﬁtability to a struggling pharmacy in the South Hills of Pittsburgh. His desire to provide personalized care to his patients led him and his wife, Jennifer, to open Asti’s South Hills Pharmacy. For the past decade, Dan has developed deep and meaningful relationships with his patients and the providers. He has assembled a team of experts in many areas of pharmaceutical care, which has earned Asti’s the reputation of being a premier pharmacy destination in Southwestern Pennsylvania. Dan and his wife, Jennifer, reside in Peter’s Township where they enjoy sports and spending time with friends and family.

Anthony L. Bucci Professional Profile For 20 years, Mr. Anthony “Tony” Bucci has been the chairman and chief executive officer of MARC, one of the nation’s largest privately-held marketing communications companies. With offices in Pittsburgh, Boston, Chicago and Miami, MARC USA and MARCA Hispanic has 200 associates. After joining MARC USA in January, 1970 as an assistant account executive Tony moved steadily up the ranks to be named Chairman in 1997. Mr. Bucci is recognized as a pioneer in advertising agency management and re-engineering. Tony authored the American Association of Advertising Agencies’ Management Guide as well as numerous articles on agency structure, advertising and branding and has spoken to business groups all over the world. In addition to his role with MARC, he is currently on the board of a private equity company, Eastport Holdings, and previously served on the board of Allin, a publicly traded technology company.

Professional Profile
* * *
Mr. John Daley is a seasoned professional with over a 30-year career in the law enforcement and corporate security arenas. He previously served on the curriculum Advisory Committee for Waukesha County Technical College.

He was elected to the Executive Board of the Western Pennsylvania Chapter of the FBI National Academy Associates, which is an organization of over 300 police executives who have graduated from the FBI National Academy, as well as having served as President of the FBI National Academy Associates, Wisconsin Chapter and served 5 years on the Executive Board.

## Frank Genovese – President – Cirqular, Inc
Mr. Genovese manages the day-to-day operations of Cirqular with a particular emphasis on Sales and Corporate accounts in the corrections industry. Mr. Genovese has spent the past 14 years integrating the company’s product in all aspects of corrections including secure prisons, community corrections, day reporting, pre-trial, probation, treatment and mental health.
* * *
Mr. Genovese has been a senior sales, marketing and administrative executive in the high tech sector for the past thirty years. He has managed the day-to-day operations of several start-up companies. He has managed national and international sales organizations for Pittsburgh and Silicon Valley based companies. He has held the President and CEO positions at Entrata Technologies and Tela Interactive. Prior to those positions, he was the Vice President of Sales at Serviceware and Vice President of Worldwide Sales at First Data Bank a division of the Hearst Corporation.
* * *
Mr. Genovese holds a Masters Degree in Business from Carnegie Mellon University as well as a BS in Computer Science and Languages from the University of Pittsburgh.

Daniel L. Henry, CLU Vice President Daniel L. Henry is a partner/shareholder with Henry Wealth Management (HWM), a Bridgeville, PA-based financial services firm. He holds the prestigious Chartered Life Underwriters (CLU) designation from The American College, reflecting his expertise in the area of Insurance Planning. He earned his Bachelor of Science (B.S.) degree in Business and Marketing from Indiana University of Pennsylvania. In addition to being a fully insurance licensed, Dan also holds the "Series 7-General Securities Representative Exam" and Series 63 (Uniform Securities Agent State Law Exam) securities licenses. Helping clients establish and achieve their long-term financial goals is Dan’s mission. He knows that whether a client has a need for wealth creation, wealth accumulation, wealth preservation or wealth transfer, every person and situation is unique and requires solutions that are customized, highly personal and comprehensive. Working as an independent firm, Dan is not tied to any proprietary products. Once a plan is agreed to and suitable investment and insurance solutions are implemented, plans and products are frequently reviewed. Fees are competitive and fully disclosed since HWM has always operated within a fiduciary standard. Prior to joining HWM in 2004, Dan was the owner of several Play It Again Sports franchise businesses in the tri-state area. His prior experience managing all aspects of a retail operation has significantly helped to direct the growth of HWM. Shortly after graduating from IUP, Dan married his college sweetheart Lauri, is the proud father of four children and they reside in Scott Township. He is an avid local sports fan and also active within the community. His family is very involved at Our Lady of Grace Catholic Church, where Dan also coaches their high school basketball team which competes within the Diocese of Pittsburgh Catholic Youth Organization.
* * *

* * *
Mr. Anthony Lacenere is the Senior Managing Partner and Co-Founder of iNetworks, LLC, a private equity investment fund and advisory practice headquartered in Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania. The historical focus of iNetworks is to provide funding for businesses in the healthcare and life sciences industry. iNetworks has also developed a focus on solving key problems affecting physical and cyber-security infrastructure, education affordability, and the transition towards energy efficiency and alternative fuels. iNetworks also invests in innovative green-tech management teams in the clean water, clean fuel, energy efficiency, and clean transportation sectors. Mr. Lacenere provides leadership based on extensive experience in portfolio management in venture capital and other private equity, public equity including combinations, mergers, acquisitions, roll-ups, licensing agreements, going private transactions, initial public offerings, technology, and various general management operational roles, both domestically and internationally. Prior to co founding iNetworks in 1999, Mr. Lacenere was President of MDX Fund, Inc., affiliated with Universal, Inc. (“UHS”), advising UHS and developing radiation oncology investments including imaging, diagnostics, and therapeutic projects. Prior to MDX, Mr. Lacenere focused on leveraged buyouts including going private transactions and was Vice President, Financial Affairs, and Managing Director, Investments, for AMSCO International, Inc., a NYSE multinational provider of healthcare technology products, where he was responsible for private and public equity and debt offerings and domestic and international mergers, acquisitions, and alliances. Prior to leading Amsco International’s public offering, Mr. Lacenere led healthcare acquisitions in the UK, Finland, Canada, Germany, and the United States. He also was responsible for operations at Precision Scientific, Inc., a Chicago-based life sciences equipment company owned by CS First Boston, J.P. Morgan and others together with AMSCO. In addition, Mr. Lacenere has held executive positions focused on operations, investment strategy, and mergers and acquisitions at Rockwell International and Westinghouse Electric Corporation. Mr. Lacenere began his career at the Battelle Memorial Institute, where he focused on new venture technology and development for various clients worldwide. Mr. Lacenere holds an M.S. in Business Economics from Ohio State University (Graduate Research Fellow with Distinction) and a B.S. in Economics and Finance from the University of Dayton. He also attended the US Army War College in Carlisle, PA. Mr. Lacenere serves on numerous Boards, and is a Board Member of Magee Women’s Research Institute, the research arm of Magee Women’s Hospital, a UPMC affiliated hospital. Mr. Lacenere is a dual citizen with Italy.

Jim Manion
* * *
Professional Profile Mr. Jim Manion is a lifelong entrepreneur and body builder. Jim is currently the President of the International Federation of Body Builders (“IFBB”), which was created in 1946 in Montreal, Canada. The IFBB annually holds more than 2,500 competitions at the local, national, regional, continental and World Championships levels. Jim is also the Owner and President of the National Physique Committee (“NPC”). These highly regarded regulatory bodies oversee the sport of body building. NPC boasts over 20,000 participants. For decades, Jim has been instrumental in the oversight and creation of body building events world-wide in over 20 countries including the US, Canada, Vietnam, China, Russia, and Brazil. Over the years, Jim has generated over 500 jobs and hundreds of millions of revenue of state and local economies. In addition to his significant commitment to the sport of body building, Jim supports a wide array of local and state charities to encourage youth sports participation and community action. Through the 100’s of charitable boxing events hosted nationwide the IFBB provides an avenue for at risk and troubled teens to become involved. Mr. Manion has also sponsored events for local police and fire departments across the country. In 2001, Jim was inducted into the IFBB Hall of Fame and joined such prior honorees as former California Governor, Arnold Schwarzenegger. A native Pennsylvanian, Jim and his wife Debbie make their home in Pittsburgh. Career Overview International Federation of Body Building President National Physique Committee Owner RTKL 708(b)(11)RTKL 708(b)(11)

John W. Paul
* * *
Professional Profile
* * *
Mr. John Paul b r i n g s over 45 years of executive experience leading many of the highly respected health care organizations across Western Pennsylvania, highlighted by his 30 year career with University of Pittsburgh Medical Center and his tenure as the first President and CEO of Allegheny Health Network (AHN). Under his leadership, Mr. Paul became the second largest healthcare provider system in Western Pennsylvania. The AHN like UPMC had many successes under John Paul’s leadership, including significant financial improvements, clinical expansion and enhanced quality and reputation. John is a 1972 cum laude graduate of IUP with a bachelor’s degree in Business and Economics. Mr. Paul continued his studies in the Executive MBA program at the University of Pittsburgh, Joseph M. Katz School of Business and graduated with honors in 1984.
* * *
Mr. Paul has been growth-focused and demonstrated an unusual ability to achieve a healthy and aggressive balance between risk taking and rewards. Throughout his career, Mr. Paul has been known for his business acumen and creating win/win scenarios among key groups and stakeholders.

Terrance “Tuffy” Shallenberger
* * *
Professional Profile
* * *
Mr. Terrance “Tuffy” Shallenberger has over 30 years’ experience in the construction business in Southwestern Pennsylvania. Tuffy is a dedicated business owner with a key focus on providing stable, good paying jobs for his team. Corporate Overview Shallenberger Construction Owner / Operator Shallenberger Construction, Inc. was established in 1971 as a general contractor and project management company. Tuffy Shallenberger assumed the Owner/Operator role in 1991. Since assuming the role, Tuffy has grown the operation from a 3,000 sq. ft location with approximately 300 employees to ten times greater. When fully operational Shallenberger Construction now employs approximately 300 people and has a nearly 30,000 sq. ft facility.
* * *
Community Activities Shallenberger SportsPlex The Shallenberger Construction, Inc. crew developed 114 acres of land the club had purchased 10 years earlier. It had been the soccer club’s goal to make the land their home field. Today, hundreds of youth practice and play at Shallenberger SportsPlex, a lighted facility that houses a playground and concession stand. Harry Clark’s Indian Creek Valley Railroad Display Through a partnership with the Fayette County Cultural Trust, Tuffy brought the 25 foot by 50 foot display to his hometown of Connellsville painstakingly by truck and built a building around it on a vacant lot.
* * *
The building known as the Connellsville Canteen is representative of the former B & O Railroad Station in Connellsville where more than a half million military service members were served refreshments by volunteers of the Connellsville Canteen during World War II. The Connellsville Canteen is used for events and houses not only the train, but a museum and coffee shop as well. The Aaron’s Building Tuffy and his crew painstakingly took on the task of revitalizing the Aaron’s Building to it’s original splendor. Of all the projects Tuffy has done, he said it has been the restoration of the Aaron’s building that has given him the most energy. “To see something that was horrendous become what is now breathtaking. It is absolutely beautiful.
* * *

Doris was named Chair of the Federal Reserve Bank of Cleveland in January 2023. ## Eugene “Gene” P. Beard
Eugene “Gene” P. Beard is a business investor and philanthropist. Formerly Chairmen and CEO of Westport Asset Fund, Inc.
* * *
Gene attended North Catholic High School where he is a member of the Hall of Fame and is an alumnus of Duquesne University, receiving both his Bachelor of Science Degree (B’59) and Masters in Business Administration Degree (MBA’61) from the Business school where he received the Ford Foundation Fellowship in business administration and economics. He was the recipient of an honorary degree of Doctor of Ethics in Business Leadership from Duquesne in May of 1988 and in 2014 received an Honorary Degree from Carlow University.
* * *
He was Vice Chairman, Finance & Operations and Chief Financial Officer of the Interpublic Group of Companies (IPG). He retired from IPG in 2001.
* * *
In 1997 Gene was named as an Independent Director to the Old Westbury Fund, Inc. Mr. Beard retired as Chairman of the Old Westbury Fund, Inc., in 2015.
* * *
During his career Mr. Beard has served as either a Director or Board member for Brown Brothers, Harriman, Mattel Corporation, Catalina Marketing Corporation, Huntworth, Plc, Scandant, Plc and Marc USA. He has served on the Advisory Board of the New York Stock Exchange (NYSE) and the Wharton Entrepreneurial School at the University of Pennsylvania.
* * *
Mr. Beard has established numerous scholarships and in both the academic and medical communities. He established the Beard Graduate and Faculty Fellowship Programs for Ethics in the Professions at Harvard University.
* * *
At North Catholic High School his alma mater, has provided scholarships for students as well as donating the Hall of Fame Center for Outstanding Alumni.
* * *
At his college alma mater, Duquesne University, his gifts established scholarships for business students; fellowship and other funding for business faculty; awards for international study, ethics, and sustainability; and resources to fuel faculty scholarship and innovation.
* * *
At Carlow University he established the “Rose Marie Beard Women of Spirit Award” to honor his mother. Over the course of 15 years this award has provided more than 80 women scholarships to complete their college education.
* * *
Mr. Beard established the Eugene and Nancy Jones Beard Learning Center for Doctor’s and Staff at Norwalk Hospital in Norwalk, CT. which is part of Nuvance Heath as well as the Nancy Jones Beard Cancer Radiology Center. At Yale Cardiology in Branford, CT he provided funding for the Eugene & Nancy Beard Heart and Vascular Center.
* * *
At Cleveland Clinic Florida his donations helped to start the Eugene P. and Nancy J. Beard, Nuclear Heart and Imaging Center as well as the Beard Education and Leadership Program Center for Doctors and Staff.
* * *

Mark K. German

Professional Profile
* * *
Mr. Mark K German is a business founder, inventor and visionary of the automotive industry. Mark spent his nearly 40-year career launching business ventures and inventing state of the art products to improve the durability and extend the life of personal and commercial vehicles. Mr. German’s venture International Liner has been in business for over 25 years and is largely credited for bringing the North American idea of the Truck Bed Liner protection to the world markets. Annual revenues are approximately $3 million dollars. Mark holds over 25 domestic and world-wide patents. Mr. German and his wife, Terri Falconi German, spend their time between Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania and Naples, Florida.

13 Rev. April 2024
* * *
Section 5. Significant Changes (Scoring Method: Pass/Fail)
* * *
A. Significant Changes Explain in the box below any significant changes (e.g. litigation, product recalls, decreased production, capital sufficiency concerns, etc.) since the initial permit or latest permit renewal. Attach additional documentation as a PDF file if you need more space or have supporting documentation. On June 6 th, Whole Plants received a Notice of Deficiency from the Bureau that contains several erroneous conclusions based on false claims by the UFCW. Whole Plants plans to appeal the NoD because at no time was Whole Plants in breach of the Neutrality Agreement through its expiration date. The Neutrality Agreement was executed in 2018 and was included in the original application submitted by Whole Plants for its G/P Permt. The Neutrality included a 3 -year term of expiration, and therefore the DOH was notified of the expiration of the Agreement at the time the application was filed. Although Whole Plants and the UFCW continued to communicate and discuss how Whole Plants might help the UFCW organize a union for it semployees, Whole Plants made it clear to the UFCW that it was under no obligation to assist the UFCW form a union because the Neutrality Agreement expired, but would not oppose the formation of a union if the employees of Whole Plants wanted the UFCW or any other union to represent them. Whole Plan ts complied with all terms of the Neutrality Agreement through its expiration. Although the UFCW disputed the expiration of the Neutrality Agreement and requested an arbitration hearing, on May 30, 2024 the UFCW and Whole Plants Settled the dispute (in writing) and agreed to the same terms as were in the original agreement starting on May 30, 2024 through November 1, 2024.
* * *
Providing significant changes in this application does not negate the duty to report requirements of 28 Pa. Code §1141a.38. During this application process, the applicant shall notify the Bureau in writing of any change in facts or circumstances reflected in this application submitted to the Bureau, or any newly discovered or occurring fact or circumstance which would have been included in this application if known at the time the application was submitted.
* * *
B. Affidavit Sign and attach the Affidavit of Significant Changes. Execute the affidavit and save as a PDF file.
* * *
Section 6. Release Authorization (Scoring Method: Pass/Fail)

I, James Smith, the undersigned, hereby certify that I am the CEO of Whole Plants LLC and am authorized to execute this affidavit on behalf of A pplicant filing this Application for Approval of an Act 63 of 2023 permit. I hereby certify and acknowledge the following statements:
* * *
• The information disclosed in this application is accurate. • The Applicant disclosed all information known by applicant related to securities agreements involving the applicant or related persons or entities. • The Applicant will not enter into a change of control transaction with a person for at least one year after the primary dispensary facility or grower/processor facility is deemed operational by the Bureau of Medical Marijuana (Bureau), unless the person is a diverse group (securities sale prohibition period). • The Applicant acknowledges that the securities sale prohibition period is a blackout period, wherein the Applicant may not solicit, negotiate, or prepare an agreement to enter into a change of control transaction, and does not end until one year after operationalization. • The Applicant is required to report to the Bureau as part of Applicant’s duty to report any change of control transaction and any change in control in the form and manner prescribed by the Bureau, including reporting to the Bureau a potential change of control transaction with a diverse group before the securities sale prohibition period ends. • The Applicant acknowledges that entering into a change of control transaction before the securities sale prohibition period ends and with a person other than a diverse group will result in a void agreement between the parties, will be a violation of 35 P.S. § 10231.618(a)(4), and will be considered submission of falsified information in this application. • The Applicant acknowledges that the Bureau is held harmless of liability for any losses resulting from a void agreement as a result of entering into a change of control transaction during the securities sale prohibition period and with a person other than a diverse group. This proposal is not intended to be a binding contract (except as expressly stated herein in the Confidentiality provision), a lease or an offer to lease, but is intended only to provide the basis for negotiations for a binding lease document (the “Lease”) between Richard Paul (“Landlord”) and Whole Plants, LLC (“Tenant”). Zoning Compliance Location: 1600 Cochran Road, Pittsburgh, PA 15220 (“Property”) County: Allegheny Municipality: Scott Township Zoning District: General Commercial (C-2) Zoning Permitted: Yes, by Conditional Use Explanation: As depicted by the red “X” in the enclosed Zoning Map of Scott Township, the Property is located within the C-2 Zoning District. Scott Township’s zoning ordinance provides that a medical marijuana dispensary may be permitted through a Conditional Use permit in the C-2 Zoning District. Attached are the relevant portions from the Township’s Zoning Ordinance indicating a medical marijuana dispensary may be permitted. Whole Plants has reached out to Scott Township regarding the zoning approval process and is in the process of submitting a n application for a Conditional Use permit. Whole Plants anticipates submitting for the Conditional Use permit by August 1, 2024 and anticipates that zoning approval can be obtained by September 1, 2024.

2. An on-site manager will be available at all times during the facility’s esta blished operating hours. 3. No activities other than rental of storage space and pick-up and deposit of storage items shall be allowed on the premises. Customers shall not be permitted to operate a business or equipment within a self-storage facility. 4. Ingress and egress shall be from an arterial or collector street. 5. Access driveways shall be a minimum width of 24 feet and paved with an impervious surface. 6. A buffer with a minimum width of 20 feet shall be provided around the perimeter of the site. The buffer shall be planted in accordance with the requirements of Section 3-110.5 of this Ordinance. 7. The facility shall be completely secured with fencing around the perimeter in accordance with the regulations of Section 3-101.7 of this Ordinance. 8. A fire hydrant shall be provided on site with the location to be determined and approved by the applicable water authority and fire department. 9. No storage may take place outside of the building. 10. Self-storage units shall not have water or sanitary sewer service. 11. No hazardous materials or substances are permitted in self-storage units beyond the allowance of the Township Construction Code or Fire Code.
* * *
D. Medical Marijuana Dispensary
* * *
1. A medical marijuana dispensary shall provide proof of registration with the Department of Health or proof that registration has been sought and is pending approval, and shall at all times maintain a valid, accurate, and up to date registration with the Pennsylvania Department of Health. Should registration be denied or revoked at any time, any conditional use approval shall immediately become void. 2. A medical marijuana dispensary shall at all times operate in compliance with all Pennsylvania Department of Health regulations pertaining to such facilities. 3. A medical marijuana dispensary shall not be operated or maintained on a parcel within 500 feet from the nearest point on the property line of a residential use or a parcel containing a public or private school, day care center, place of worship, public park, or community center. 4. A medical marijuana dispensary must operate entirely within an indoor, enclosed, and secure facility. No exterior sales or no sidewalk displays shall be permitted. No drive through, drop off, or pick up services shall be permitted. 5. No use of medical marijuana shall be permitted on the premises. 6. A medical marijuana dispensary shall have a single secure public entrance and shall implement appropriate security measures to deter and prevent the theft and unauthorized entrance into areas containing medical marijuana.
* * *
E. Medical Marijuana Grower / Processor
* * *
1. A medical marijuana grower/processor shall provide proof of registration with the Pennsylvania Department of Health or proof that registration has been sought and is pending approval, and shall at all times maintain a vaild, accurate, and up to date registration with the Pennsylvania Department of

WHOLE PLANTS’ DISPENSARY EMPLOYEE QUALIFICATIONS, DESCRIPTION OF DUTIES, AND TRAINING
* * *
## – EMPLOYEE QUALIFICATIONS AND DUTIES (SECTIONS 9A
AND 9B)
* * *
CHIEF EXECUTIVE OFFICER Duties • Ensure all documentation is properly filed to assure compliance with all laws and regulations. • Work with the Board to determine the Whole Plants’ values, mission, vision, and short and long-term goals. • Inform the Board of both the current operating state and relevant factoring influencing the future of Whole Plants. • Ensure all company policies are enforced equitably. • Provide macro-management of all Whole Plants’ activities, including the day-to-day operations, and assuring a continuously functioning and efficient organization. • Ensure consistent product creation and overall company stability, through proper design of standards, controls, and continuous evaluation procedures. • Ensure a stable and safe work environment which cultivates internal growth of quality staff and volunteers, starting at the hiring process and continuing throughout the years of employment. • Assure the Board of proper staffing and financial recommendations. • Negotiate and maintain professional contracts and salary structures. • Create a specific accountability structure for management and ensure its utilization for performance evaluations. • Help the Board develop its role and relevant accountabilities, for both the Board members and their committees. Work alongside Chair of the Board to ensure the Board is fulfilling its governance functions and facilitating the peak performance by the Board on long-term strategic goals. • Maintain the fulfillment of the Board’s due diligence to ensure timely attention to pertinent issues.
* * *
• Ensure all goods and services are produced efficiently and cost-effectively. Determine the fiscal stability of the company, through the review of budgets, reports, and relevant audits. • Help the Board evaluate financials in reference to completion of short and long-term goals. • Properly utilize marketing and communications resources to integrate Whole Plants into the local community. • Fulfill the role of advocate, both in the public and private sectors, for all issues pertaining to Whole Plants’. • Initiate, develop, and maintain cooperative relationships with government officials. Work to foster a responsible relationship with government officials. Qualifications  Minimum 10 years executive or director level experience of company in healthcare sector.  Minimum 5 years executive experience for a non-profit or charitable organization.  Master’s in business administration.  Executive-level experience in cannabis industry preferred. CHIEF FINANCIAL OFFICER Duties • Ensure proper functionality of finance and accounting departments, while ensuring growth and extending financial decision making throughout company infrastructure. • In charge of accounting, responsible fiscal planning, analysis, budgeting, internal controls, financial systems, auditing, reporting, treasury decisions, insurance relations, and tax compliance. • Will work with the Department of Revenue to discuss tax clearance and remittance issues. • Responsible for producing monthly and quarterly fiscal updates for the Board of Directors, external auditors, analysts, and all other external entities that require financials. • Work alongside CEO and senior management to develop and implement business plans and operating initiatives. • Work with CEO and senior management to facilitate any major transactions including capital raises, debt, mergers, acquisitions, and joint ventures. • Define standards, policies, procedures, measures, and organizational enhancements to comply with financial goals. • Create and define all financial reporting and business analytics. Develop and implement a system for continuous fiscal reporting and analysis. • Responsible for all real estate agreements. • Utilize analytics to drive operations, growth, and functionality. • Document and translate operational results into financial report.
* * *
Qualifications  Advanced work in finance or economics MBA preferred.  10+ year finance experience required.  Experience developing and managing financial models.  Experience negotiating real estate purchases and leasing.  Executive-level experience in cannabis industry preferred.
* * *
CHIEF OPERATING OFFICER Duties • Responsible for consistent and effective implementation of operational systems and processes that make effective use of organizational resources. • Oversee and develop quality controls for current and future products, ensuring consistent and ever-improving quality. • Create a work environment in which employees are invested to their organization while maintaining a sense of pride and accomplishment. • Create an environment in which product quality ensures customer satisfaction. • Direct the human resources department in the process of hiring and maintaining employee relations to ensure smooth and continuous operations. • Develop clear and achievable requirements and hold employees accountable to them. • Motivate and facilitate teamwork and a positive company environment. • Develop and maintain positive relations with employees, regulatory agencies, contractors, and other applicable parties, while fostering a high level of collaboration to coordinate activities, review work, exchange information, and resolve problems. • Promote collaboration with various stakeholders to garner optimal results. • Provide leadership and actively participate in the development and implementation of strategic, operational planning. • Utilize forecasting and planning processes to identify capital and technological acquisitions alongside program development opportunities which achieve desired growth related to capacity and quality of products and services offered. • Effectively communicate company goals to the relevant employee and community groups. Conduct routine employee discussions to be informed of the issues that employees are facing and while ensuring that issues are addressed timely. Qualifications  MBA preferred.  5+ years of experience in supply chain management and business operations and organization.  Strong business/financial acumen/Ability to work effectively in a matrix environment.  Executive-level experience in cannabis industry preferred.
* * *
CHIEF DEVELOPMENT OFFICER Duties • Serve as the leader of research and development team. • Maintain technical currency and apply this knowledge to evaluate new and emerging technologies. • Maintain and evaluate physical and software systems to retain and improve operational efficiency. • Ensure proper function of patient infrastructure. • Macro manage the day-to-day dispensary operations to insure correct implementation of the RFID tracking, scanning, and collection of information. Qualifications • Bachelor’s Degree • 5+ years of experience in product development team • 5+ years engineering experience COMPLIANCE OFFICER Duties • Review all company policies and procedures regularly to ensure compliance with relevant laws and industry standards on a continuing basis. • Coordinate with other department heads to guide development of new policies and procedures. • Prepare reports to all relevant regulatory bodies as necessary. • Coordinate with outside legal counsel as necessary to review contracts and permitting requirements. Qualifications  Bachelor’s Degree in Public Administration or Political Science or J.D. (preferable).  7+ years of experience reading and interpreting regulations and working within an FDA regulatory framework.  Experience in public affairs is preferable. Experience as an attorney is a plus.  Executive-level experience in cannabis industry preferred.
* * *
HEAD OF HUMAN RESOURCES Duties • Will discuss with the Department of Labor and Industry, worker compensation issues. • Will ensure all employees receive relevant training. • Will ensure all employees maintain a high level of personal hygiene and are of at least 21 years of age. • Work alongside Chief Operating Officer in all human resource activities including recruiting, selection and retention, hiring and termination,
* * *
administering compensation, training and development, counseling, employee relations, conflict resolution, performance evaluations, and administering employment policies and procedures. • Oversee and coordinate review and updates to job descriptions and continuous performance evaluations. • Maintain current knowledge of HR best practices, policies, programs, regulations, industry trends, new developments, and applicable laws regarding human resources. • Provide advice and counsel to management team and employee concerns. • Coordinate, and oversee all recruiting and hiring activities. • Manage and systematize new employee process and exit interviews. • Monitor and maintain all employee files and records. • Complete selected benefit worksheets and documents. • Evaluate and report on recurring employee compliance obligations (training, introductory evaluations, annual evaluations, Annual TB testing, license renewals, etc...) • Assist with as well as create management reports for Chief Operating Officer. • Manage employee grievance and complaint procedures Ensure employees are aware of their rights including those dictated by OSHA. Qualifications  Bachelor’s or Master’s degree in Business Administration preferred  Professional Human Resources Certification
* * *
## - MANAGEMENT
DISPENSARY MANAGER
* * *
Duties • Serve as the Designated Representative (DR) to dispensaries and the Department of Health. • Interact with and assist patients. • Oversee inventory management, recalls, ordering, receiving, and disposal of product. • Responsible for ensuring proper record keeping. • Oversee and coordinate with Security Personnel to ensure safety of personnel and product. • Oversee Pharmacists to ensure proper and efficient treatment of patients. • Oversee, delegate, and manage tasks for Dispensary Technicians to ensure the dispensary functions efficiently and properly each day. Qualifications  Bachelor’s degree preferred.  Minimum 3 years in management position which required regular interface with FDA, Department of Health, or other food/drug regulatory authority.  Experience with inventory management and acquisition.
* * *
 Computer skill and Point of Sale register experience. 3 – EMPLOYEES PHARMACIST Duties • Meet with and advise Medical Marijuana patients of proper and best course of treatment. • Provide patient consultations to discuss primary care physician’s medical Recommendations. • Discuss benefits and side effects of the medicine. • Working with HHR to develop educational training and materials for employees. • Develop educational materials for patients. • Other tasks as assigned by the Dispensary Manager or the executive team. Qualifications  B.S. Pharmacy required, PharmD preferred.  Licensed pharmacist in the State of Pennsylvania.  Experience working with patients preferred.  Ability to learn and adapt in a new and changing healthcare field.  Computer skill and Point of Sale register experience. SECURITY PERSONNEL Duties • Verify identification of all individuals that enter the dispensary. • Work with the Dispensary Manager to coordinate employee emergency drills. • Oversee the Dispensary Manager in processing and inventorying deliveries and movements of medical marijuana. • Ensuring on a day-to-day basis that all security measures are properly functioning. • Any other task that is assigned by the Dispensary Manager or COO related to security. Qualifications  Pass Level II background check.  At least 21 years of age.  Must possess the ability to make independent decisions when circumstances warrant such action..  Previous work as a Security Guard preferred.  ACT 235 Certification required. DISPENSARY TECHNICIAN Duties • Interact with and dispense medicine to patients • Follow all Company policies and SOPs to ensure safe, sanitary, and effective service and medicine.
* * *
• Maintain all necessary certifications and training needed to dispense medical marijuana medicines. • Complete any other tasks as assigned by the Dispensary Manager or COO. Qualifications  At least 21 years of age  Computer skill and Point of Sale register experience ADMINISTRATIVE ASSISTANT Duties • Perform administrative duties as directed by the Dispensary Manager Qualifications  High School Diploma  Basic Computer Skills necessary  At least 21 years of age
* * *
## - EMPLOYEE TRAINING (SECTION 9C)
Pursuant to 28 Pa. Code §1141a.48, all principals and employees of Whole Plants (“Company”)
* * *
shall complete the Department of Health’s (“DOH”) mandatory 2-hour training. All principals shall complete training prior to the dispensary becoming operational; all employees will complete the training within 90 day of the start of his/her employment. Per §1141a.48(b), the Company recognizes that DOH’s training includes the following topics:
* * *
• General overview of the Medical Marijuana Act and DOH regulations; • Proper handling of medical marijuana products that enter the dispensary; • Proper recordkeeping; • Prevention and detection of product diversion; • Best practice security procedures; and • Best practice safety procedures, including: medical, fire, criminal actor emergencies.
* * *
The Company shall facilitate attendance for this required training by offering rides (if DOH holds it in person) or providing the technological means to complete it online. Further, per §1161a.48(c), Whole Plants shall retain as part of its recordkeeping SOPs (discussed in Section 17) attendance records and other evidence that each principal and employee complied with the mandatory training required by §1141a.48(a).
* * *
In addition to the 2-hour training required of all principals and employees, Whole Plants’ on-site pharmacist (or physician) shall complete the 4-hour training required by §1161a.25(c). These medical professionals shall also be required to maintain his/her professional license by completing any Continuing Medical Education (CME) that are required by the professional’s respective licensing board in Pennsylvania. In addition to the required training, Whole Plants’ will be implementing a dispensary-specific training regimen for all new hires. All new employees shall be required to successfully complete
* * *
Company training within 60 days of hiring—this training will include some on -the-job training and an assessment of SOP/employee manual knowledge and understanding. Evidence of the successful completion of this training will be retained in the employee’s personnel file and will be maintained in accordance with our recordkeeping policies described in Section 17 of this application. Specifically, this training shall include:
* * *
• Opening/closing procedures; • Inventory management protocols – including the importance of logging everything in DOH’s seed-to-sale tracking system per §1161a.39 and into the Company’s inventory system through scanning RFID on each product; • Reviewing and confirming a medical marijuana patient ID card per §1161a.24; • Forms of medical marijuana and lawful methods to consume per the Medical Marijuana Act (“MMA”), 35 P.S. §10231.303; • Information about the products offered at the dispensary to assist with patient selection, including the risks, benefits, and other pros/cons about medical marijuana generally and each specific product offering; • Qualifying serious medical conditions per the MMA; • Procedures to conduct a dispensing transactions, including generating receipts and providing safety inserts per §1161a.27 and §1161a.28; • Dispensary storage requirements in accordance with §1161a.33; • Sanitation and safety protocols to ensure a clean, sanitary, and safe facility per §1161a.34; • Protocols to receive and ship medical marijuana products, including transport manifests and detecting product diversion pursuant to §1161a.35, §1161a.36, and §1161a.37; • Protocols for customer complaints, product returns, and product recalls in accord with §1161a.38; • Cash handling procedures; • Access privileges; and • Security and emergency training that is in addition to DOH’s required training and which is site-specific to the Company’s dispensary.
* * *
Our training is comprehensive and led by individuals with actual experience in the medical marijuana industry. Employees will be instructed on day 1 that employees will be required to strictly comply with all Company SOPs and shall be informed that failure to comply with SOPs creates a presumption of diversion. For any violation, the employee shall be required to explain their actions and demonstrate no diversion occurred. The Company shall utilize an escalating disciplinary program for violations. For most first violations, employees will be required to be re trained. A second violation may result in re-training or a more severe reprimand. A third violation may result in employee termination.
* * *
On an annual basis the Company shall require a refresher training course for all of its employees. In addition, in the event SOPs are updated or new products are received, employees shall be trained on these new protocols/products on an as-needed basis.
* * *
All employee training and employee reprimands shall be maintained by the Company in an employees’ personnel file, which shall be retained in accordance with the Company’s recordkeeping policies.
* * *

14 Rev. April 2024
* * *
Section 5. Significant Changes (Scoring Method: Pass/Fail)
* * *
A. Significant Changes Explain in the box below any significant changes (e.g. litigation, product recalls, decreased production, capital sufficiency concerns, etc.) since the initial permit or latest permit renewal. Attach additional documentation as a PDF file if you need more space or have supporting documentation. Since beginning operations in late 2017, Standard Farms has provided the Pennsylvania Medical Marijuana Program a continuous and uninterrupted supply of medical marijuana products for dispensaries and patients since March 2018. As one of the first‐round grower‐processors in operation, Standard Farms has experienced firsthand the ebbs and flows of the Program. Standard Farms has not undergone any significant changes, but has committed to supporting and growing market demands for new products. Standard Farms has undergone multiple facility alterations that have allowed for innovative, safer, and easier to dispense products to be manufactured, stored, and distributed to patients. Standard Farms has never been mandated nor initiated a product recall. Standard Farms has only recently entered into a lending contract to address capital sufficiency in support of the dispensary permit application. There has been no previous history of capital concerns within the Pennsylvania medical market.
* * *
Providing significant changes in this application does not negate the duty to report requirements of 28 Pa. Code §1141a.38. During this application process, the applicant shall notify the Bureau in writing of any change in facts or circumstances reflected in this application submitted to the Bureau, or any newly discovered or occurring fact or circumstance which would have been included in this application if known at the time the application was submitted.
* * *
B. Affidavit Sign and attach the Affidavit of Significant Changes. Execute the affidavit and save as a PDF file.
* * *
Section 6. Release Authorization (Scoring Method: Pass/Fail)
* * *
Sign and attach the Release Authorization as set forth in §1211a.24 (relating to capital requirements). Execute the affidavit and save as a PDF file. Failure to provide a release will result in the rejection of the application for approval of an Act 63 of 2023 permit.

Part B – Diversity Plan (Scoring Method: 100 Points) IN ACCORDANCE WITH SECTION 615 OF THE ACT (35 P.S. § 10231.615), AN APPLICANT SHALL INCLUDE WITH ITS APPLICATION A DIVERSITY PLAN THAT PROMOTES AND ENSURES THE INVOLVEMENT OF DIVERSE PARTICIPANTS AND DIVERSE GROUPS IN OWNERSHIP, MANAGEMENT, EMPLOYMENT, AND CONTRACTING OPPORTUNITIES. DIVERSE PARTICIPANTS INCLUDE INDIVIDUALS FROM DIVERSE RACIAL, ETHNIC AND CULTURAL BACKGROUNDS AND COMMUNITIES; WOMEN; VETERANS; AND INDIVIDUALS WITH DISABILITIES. DIVERSE GROUPS INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING BUSINESSES THAT HAVE BEEN CERTIFIED BY A THIRD-PARTY CERTIFYING ORGANIZATION OR THAT HAVE BEEN VERIFIED BY THE DEPARTMENT OF GENERAL SERVICES BUREAU OF DIVERSITY, INCLUSION AND SMALL BUSINESS OPPORTUNITIES: A DISADVANTAGED BUSINESS, MINORITY-OWNED BUSINESS, AND WOMEN-OWNED BUSINESS AS THOSE TERMS ARE DEFINED IN 74 PA. ## From: Aaron Wozniak <awozniak@springtwpberks.org>
Sent: Monday, May 20, 2024 9:55 AM Subject: [EXTERNAL] RE: 2800 State Hill RdZoning Verification Request
* * *
Good Morning,
* * *
The property of 2800 State Hill Road is located in the Township of Spring’s Planned Office/Business (PO/B) zoning district. The Township does not have a specific zoning category for medical dispensaries. We define them in our Zoning Ordinance as Retail Store. A Retail Store is a Use By Right in the PO/B zoning district.
* * *
The current/last use of the property was defined as Financial Establishment. The use of the property can be changed to another use if the new use complies with the requirements of the Township Zoning Ordinance. As an example, different uses can have different parking count requirements. A financial establishment is required to have 1 parking space per 250 square feet of building floor area plus one for every employee. A retail store is required to have 1 per 200 square feet of building floor area plus one per employee. A retail store requires more parking than a bank, unless employee counts vary significantly.
* * *
Parking space configurations and parking aisles also have requirements, and this particular property appears to have enough area to accommodate the parking layout requirements, but that is not known until it is proven by submission of an application with enough detail to establishment all applicable requirements are met. This is the information the Township has previously discussed with your group.
* * *
Also discussed were the legal requirements of a Preliminary Opinion for a zoning decision. The Township is prohibited by the Pennsylvania Municipalities Planning Code Section 916.2 from providing a zoning decision prior to the submission of a zoning or construction application. A zoning decision is subject to appeal from the general public and other entities. I cannot give you a zoning decision that can be relied on without giving the public notice that a zoning decision is being requested. A favorable decision must be published twice in a local newspaper and there are adopted fees and costs for such a decision ($1,000.00). We would also need enough information similar to a zoning/construction application to be able to offer a decision.
* * *
What I can tell you is stated above, and was stated in phone conversations. Medical cannabis is defined an ordinary retail in our Township. The property appears to have potential to comply with requirements, but that cannot be known until you submit an adequate plan showing enough information for that to be determined. The resulting decision can either be a permit or a preliminary opinion, but either method requires submission of enough information to make that decision.
* * *
Sincerely, TOWNSHIP OF SPRING J. Aaron Wozniak Zoning Officer / Building Code Official 610-678-5393, ext. 1440
* * *
